malware sends a notification to the C2 by encapsulating Mode as the field of a packet class and shipping the serialized instance.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCapture screenshots\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eJanelaRAT is capable of capturing and shipping screenshots. It defines an packet class containing three fields:\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cul\u003e\r\n\t\u003cli\u003eJanela (window, in Portuguese): Integer dictating the type of screenshot operation being requested. If Janela is set to 1, the malware captures a magnified screenshot. If Janela is set to 2, then the malware live-captures a screenshot and sends it through the C2.\u003c/li\u003e\r\n\t\u003cli\u003eMode: Integer that controls the encoding of the captured screenshot. If this field is set to a value bigger than 10, then the screenshot is encoded as a PNG, otherwise it is encoded as a JPG.\u003c/li\u003e\r\n\t\u003cli\u003eNumber: This field is not used.\u003c/li\u003e\r\n\u003c/ul\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRun in special execution modes\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eJanelaRat ships with the capability of running in special execution modes. Each execution mode affects the malware behaviour and it is identified by a label. The attacker may request the malware to operate in any of those modes.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eAs an example, when in \u003cstrong\u003e_blcoqueio_tempo_determinado\u003c/strong\u003e mode, the malware creates a new block.blq file with a limited duration in minutes. The purpose of this behaviour is to temporarily prevent the user from opening windows with specific titles. The file is created only if it doesn’t already exist in the malware directory.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eWhen in \u003cstrong\u003e_modal_inicial \u003c/strong\u003emode, the malware shows a modal dialog that forces the user to interact with the malware by disabling user interaction with the main window. The foreground image for the dialog is obtained from C2. The malware registers a hook for both keyboard and mouse events. \u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eWhen in \u003cstrong\u003e_modal_win_update \u003c/strong\u003emode, JanelaRAT displays a fake alert warning the user to not shut the system down while the Windows updates are in progress. Most likely, this allows the attacker to operate on the compromised host while the fake warning is shown to the user.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eFinally, when in \u003cstrong\u003e_modal_loading\u003c/strong\u003e, \u003cstrong\u003emodal_error\u003c/strong\u003e, or \u003cstrong\u003emodal_tocalm\u003c/strong\u003e, JanelaRAT operates in the same way: it shows an attacker-provided image to the user. The image is different in each mode, but we weren't able to obtain any of those at the time of analysis.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\n"},"fieldSidebarNavigationTitle":null}]},{"__typename":"ParagraphBlogContainer","fieldSidebarNavigationTitle":"Relationship with BX RAT","fieldReusableParagraphs":[{"__typename":"ParagraphWysiwygModule","fieldWysiwygModContent":{"__typename":"Text","value":"\u003ch2\u003eRelationship with BX RAT\u003c/h2\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eBX RAT is a malware discovered in 2014 and is a fully-fledged Remote Access Trojan (RAT). As shown in the image below, BX RAT serializes a packet instance as an array of integers. This array is later encrypted and finally compressed with a custom implementation of the LZ4 algorithm. The same we observed in JanelaRAT. The encryption algorithm, at least in this BX RAT sample, is a different one since it consists of a custom implementation of AES instead of RC4 - like in JanelaRAT.\u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003eRegardless, the two images below show the similarity between the BX RAT C2 transmission procedure (top) and the corresponding code in JanelaRAT (bottom). \u003c/p\u003e\r\n\r\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg alt=\"  BX RAT serializes a packet instance as an array of integers\" data-entity-type=\"\" data-entity-uuid=\"\"
